أما الأول فلاندراج كل شخص تحت الماهيات المعراة عن المشخصات. وأما الثاني فلجواز كون الجزئي الإضافي كلياً، وامتناع كون الجزئي الحقيقي كذلك.
القول: «الجزئي» مقول بالاشتراك على المعنى المذكور، ويسمى جزئياً حقيقياً، لأن جزئيته بالنظر إلى حقيقته المانعة من الشركة – وبإزائه «الكلّي الحقيقي»
وعلى كل أخص تحت الأعم كالإنسان بالنسبة إلى الحيوان، ويسمى جزئياً إضافياً»، لأن جزئيته بالإضافة إلى شيء آخر، وبإزائه «الكلّي الإضافي» وهو الأعم من شيء آخر.
فإن قلت : فإن الكلّي أيضاً له معنيان مختلفان : أحدهما حقيقي والآخر إضافي - على قياس الجزئي - وفيه بحث، لأن الامتياز بين الجزئي وكون أحدهما حقيقياً والآخر إضافياً أمر مكشوف على ما بينه، وأما الكلّي فليس يظهر له معنيان متمايزان كذلك، فإن معناه المتقدم الذي سماه هاهنا كلياً حقيقياً هو الصالح لفرض الاشتراك بين كثيرين، ولاشك أنه أمر نسبي لا يعقل للشيء إلا بالقياس إلى كثيرين، فإن أراد بالكلّي الإضافي هذا المعنى فليس للكلّي إذن معنيان ، وإن أراد به معنى آخر فلم لم يبينه ؟ قلت: أراد به معنی آخر، وقد بينه بقوله «وهو الأعم من شيء» ومعناه أنه الذي يندرج تحته شيء آخر ، ولا نعني بالاندراج «مايكون مندرجاً بمجرد الفرض حتى يرجع إلى المعنى الأول بعينه، بل مايكون بحسب نفس الأمر. فالكلّي الحقيقي ماصلح لأن يندرج تحته شيء آخر بحسب فرض العقل، سواء أمكن الاندراج في نفس الأمر أو لا.
والكلّيّ الأضافي ما اندرج تحته شيء آخر في نفس الأمر، فيكون أخص من الكلّي الحقيقي قطعاً بدرجتين : الأولى أن الكلي الحقيقي قد لا يمكن اندراج شيء تحته وإن لم يندرج بالفعل كما في الكليات الفرضية، ولا يتصور ذلك في الإضافي. والثانية أن الكلي الحقيقي، ربما أمكن اندراج شيء تحته وإن لم يندرج
بالفعل - لاذهناً ولا خارجاً - ولابد في الإضافي من الاندراج بالفعل. وإنما خص هذا المعنى بالإضافي لأنّ الإضافة فيه أظهر من الإضافة في المعنى الأول، وسمي الأول بالحقيقي لكونه مقابلا للجزئي الحقيقي. على أن صلاحية فرض الاشتراك بين كثيرين قديناقش في كونها إضافية وإن كان تعقلها موقوفاً على تعقل الغير؛ كما أن تعقل المنع من فرض الاشتراك بين كثيرين موقوف على تعقل الغير مع أنه ليس إضافياً، لأن تحققه لا يتوقف على تحقق الغير، وحينئذ يكون تسميته بالحقيقي ظاهرة، وعلى هذا فالجزئي الإضافي ما اندرج بالفعل تحت غيره.
ولو قلنا : الجزئي الإضافي ما أمكن اندراجه تحت شيء» كان الكلي
He said: The fourth: The particular, just as it is said for the mentioned meaning – called the real – likewise it is said for every more specific under the more general, and it is called the 'relational particular', and it is more general than the first, because every real particular is a relational particular without the reverse.
As for the first, it is because every individual is subsumed under essences stripped of individuators. As for the second, it is because it is possible for the relational particular to be universal, and it is impossible for the real particular to be so.
The statement: 'The particular' is said by homonymy for the mentioned meaning, and it is called a real particular because its particularity is with respect to its essence that prevents sharing – and opposite it is the 'real universal' – and for every more specific under the more general, such as 'human' in relation to 'animal', and it is called a 'relational particular' because its particularity is in relation to something else, and opposite it is the 'relational universal', which is more general than something else.
If you say: Then the universal also has two different meanings: one real and the other relational – on the analogy of the particular – and there is investigation in that, because the distinction between the particular and that one is real and the other relational is clear as he explained, but as for the universal, it does not appear to have two distinct meanings like that, for its preceding meaning that he called here a real universal is what is fit for the supposition of sharing among many, and there is no doubt that it is a relative matter, not understood for a thing except in relation to many. If he meant by the relational universal this meaning, then the universal does not have two meanings, but if he meant another meaning, then why did he not clarify it? I say: He meant another meaning, and he clarified it by his saying 'It is more general than a thing', and its meaning is that something else is subsumed under it, and we do not mean by subsumption 'what is subsumed merely by supposition' such that it would revert to the first meaning itself, but rather what is in accordance with actual reality. So the real universal is what is fit for something else to be subsumed under it according to the supposition of the mind, whether actual subsumption is possible or not.
And the relational universal is that under which something else is actually subsumed, so it is definitely more specific than the real universal in two degrees: First, the real universal may not be possible for anything to be subsumed under it even if not actually subsumed, as in hypothetical universals, and this is not conceivable for the relational universal. Second, the real universal may possibly have something subsumed under it even if not actually subsumed – neither mentally nor externally – while in the relational universal actual subsumption is necessary. This meaning was specified as relational because the relation is more apparent in it than in the first meaning, and the first was called real because it is the opposite of the real particular. Moreover, the fitness for the supposition of sharing among many may be disputed as being relational, even though its conceivement depends on the conceivement of the other; just as the conceivement of the prevention of the supposition of sharing among many depends on the conceivement of the other while it is not relational, because its actuality does not depend on the actuality of the other. Then its being called real is apparent, and on this basis, the relational particular is that which is actually subsumed under something else.
And if we said: The relational particular is that which can be subsumed under something, then the universal
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage defines the real particular and relational particular, and clarifies the relationship between them. It opens with the statement that the term 'particular' is used in two senses: the real particular (al-juz'i al-haqiqi), which is the individual that cannot be predicated of many due to its essence, and the relational particular (al-juz'i al-idafi), which is anything more specific than something else, such as 'human' in relation to 'animal'. The author explains that every real particular is a relational particular (since every individual is subsumed under genera and species), but not every relational particular is a real particular, because a relational particular can itself be universal (e.g., 'human' is a relational particular relative to 'animal', but it is a universal relative to individuals). The opposite terms are the real universal (al-kulli al-haqiqi) and the relational universal (al-kulli al-idafi).

The passage then addresses an objection: one might think the universal also has two meanings on analogy with the particular. The objector argues that the real universal is already a relative notion (fit for supposition of sharing among many), so what would a relational universal add? The answer explains that the relational universal is not the same as the real universal; it is that under which something else is actually subsumed in reality, not merely in supposition. The real universal is only potentially fit for subsumption, whether or not actual subsumption occurs (e.g., a hypothetical universal like 'phoenix' may not have actual instances). The relational universal requires actual subsumption (e.g., 'animal' actually subsumes 'human'). The relational universal is therefore more specific than the real universal. The passage then notes that the real universal might be considered relational because its conceivement depends on the other, but the author argues it is not truly relational because its actuality does not depend on the actuality of the other. The same reasoning applies to the relational particular: it is that which is actually subsumed under something else. The passage ends with a conditional statement about defining the relational particular as that which can be subsumed, which would make the universal also a particular—but this is a critical refinement not fully developed.

Key Terms
الجزئي الحقيقي
الجزئي الإضافي
الكلي الحقيقي
الكلي الإضافي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is true?
A) Every real particular is a relational particular, but not every relational particular is a real particular.
B) Every relational particular is a real particular, but not every real particular is a relational particular.
C) Real particulars and relational particulars are mutually exclusive.
D) The two terms are synonymous.

Key Takeaway
The term 'particular' in logic has two senses: the individual (real) and the more specific concept (relational); the latter is broader and includes universals.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
1. Classify the following as real particular, relational particular, or both: a) Zayd b) human c) animal d) 'this specific horse'.
?
2. Explain in your own words why every real particular is a relational particular, but not every relational particular is a real particular, using an example from fiqh.

The Real and Relational Universal: Resolving an Objection
Author addresses objection about universal having two meanings, refines distinction based on actuality vs. potentiality

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate the real universal from the relational universal and explain why the real universal is not merely relational despite its conceptual dependence on others.

Core Idea
The real universal is defined by potential fitness, not actual subsumption.

The objector raises a critical point: if the universal has two meanings on analogy with the particular, then the real universal already seems relational. The author responds by clarifying that the real universal is only fit for subsumption by mental supposition, while the relational universal requires actual subsumption in reality. This refinement deepens our understanding of universality in Islamic logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Find the interrogative sentence beginning with 'فإن قلت'. The objector claims the universal should also have two meanings, but the real universal appears relational, so there may be no distinct second meaning.
2
Extract the author's response
The author ('قلت') asserts there is a second meaning and it is given by 'وهو الأعم من شيء', meaning that under which something else is actually subsumed, not merely by supposition.
3
Compare the two universals
Real universal: fit for subsumption in the mind, even if no actual instances (e.g., 'phoenix'). Relational universal: actually has subordinates in reality (e.g., 'animal' subsumes 'human').
4
Understand the two degrees of difference
The author lists two reasons why the real universal is more general: (1) it may have no possible instances (hypothetical), (2) it may have possible instances but not actual. The relational universal requires actual instances.

Real vs. Relative Universal: The Core Distinction
Defines haqiqi and idafi universal with two degrees of distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the real universal (kulli haqiqi) and the relative universal (kulli idafi) based on the mode of subsumption.

Core Idea
The real universal requires only mental possibility; the relative universal demands actual subsumption.

This passage clarifies a subtle but crucial distinction within the category of the universal. While the real universal is defined by its potential to be shared, the relative universal has an actual instance under it. Understanding this distinction sharpens your ability to classify terms in Islamic disciplines.

Guided Path
1
Locate the definitions
Find the two definitions in the Arabic: one for real universal (al-kulli al-haqiqi) and one for relative universal (al-kulli al-idafi). Note the key phrases: 'fit for assumption of sharing' vs 'more general than a thing'.
2
Identify the objector's challenge
The passage raises an objection: if the real universal is already relative (because it involves relation to many), then there are not two distinct meanings. Understand the objection.
The objector assumes that 'relative' means any relation to many, but the author argues for a stronger relation.
3
Extract the commentator's resolution
The commentator explains that the relative universal is different because it requires actual subsumption, not just mental possibility. Confirm the two degrees of difference.
The two degrees are detailed in the next part of the passage.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مباحث الكلي والجزئي
معنيي حقيقي والآخر إضافي - على قياس الجزئي - وفيه بحث، لأن الامتياز بين الجزئي وكون أحدهما حقيقياً والآخر إضافياً أمر مكشوف على ما بينه، وأما الكلّي فليس يظهر له معنيان متمايزان كذلك، فإن معناه المتقدم الذي سماه هاهنا كلياً حقيقياً هو الصالح لفرض الاشتراك بين كثيرين، ولاشك أنه أمر نسبي لا يعقل للشيء إلا بالقياس إلى كثيرين، فإن أراد بالكلّي الإضافي هذا المعنى فليس للكلّي إذن معنيان ، وإن أراد به معنى آخر فلم لم يبينه ؟ قلت: أراد به معنی آخر، وقد بينه بقوله «وهو الأعم من شيء» ومعناه أنه الذي يندرج تحته شيء آخر ، ولا نعني بالاندراج «مايكون مندرجاً بمجرد الفرض حتى يرجع إلى المعنى الأول بعينه، بل مايكون بحسب نفس الأمر. فالكلّي الحقيقي ماصلح لأن يندرج تحته شيء آخر بحسب فرض العقل، سواء أمكن الاندراج في نفس الأمر أو لا.
والكلّيّ الأضافي ما اندرج تحته شيء آخر في نفس الأمر، فيكون أخص من الكلّي الحقيقي قطعاً بدرجتين : الأولى أن الكلي الحقيقي قد لا يمكن اندراج شيء تحته وإن لم يندرج بالفعل كما في الكليات الفرضية، ولا يتصور ذلك في الإضافي. والثانية أن الكلي الحقيقي، ربما أمكن اندراج شيء تحته وإن لم يندرج بالعمل - لاذهناً ولا خارجاً - ولابد في الإضافي من الاندراج بالفعل. وإنما خص هذا المعنى بالإضافي لأنّ الإضافة فيه أظهر من الإضافة في المعنى الأول، وسمي الأول بالحقيقي لكونه مقابلا للجزئي الحقيقي. على أن صلاحية فرض الاشتراك بين كثيرين قديناقش في كونها إضافية وإن كان تعقلها موقوفاً على تعقل الغير؛ كما أن تعقل المنع من فرض الاشتراك بين كثيرين موقوف على تعقل الغير مع أنه ليس إضافياً، لأن تحققه لا يتوقف على تحقق الغير، وحينئذ يكون تسميته بالحقيقي ظاهرة، وعلى هذا فالجزئي الإضافي ما اندرج بالفعل تحت غيره.
Topics of the Universal and Particular. Two meanings: real and relative – on the analogy of the particular. There is a discussion, because the distinction between the particular and that one of them is real and the other relative is something manifest as he explained. As for the universal, it does not appear to have two distinct meanings likewise. For its preceding meaning, which he calls here the real universal, is that which is fit for assuming sharing among many. No doubt it is a relative matter, not conceived for the thing except in relation to many. If he means by the relative universal this meaning, then the universal does not have two meanings. But if he means another meaning, why did he not explain it? I say: He meant another meaning, and he explained it by his saying: 'It is the more general than a thing.' Its meaning is that something else is subsumed under it. We do not mean by subsumption 'what is subsumed merely by assumption, so that it returns to the same first meaning, but what is in reality. So the real universal is that which is fit for something else to be subsumed under it by assumption of the mind, whether subsumption is possible in reality or not. The relative universal is that under which something else is subsumed in reality. So it is definitely more specific than the real universal by two degrees: First, the real universal may have no possibility of subsumption of something under it even if not actually subsumed, as in assumed universals, and that is not conceivable for the relative. Second, the real universal may have possibility of subsumption of something under it even if not actually subsumed – neither mentally nor externally – while in the relative subsumption must be actual. He specifically called this meaning 'relative' because the relation in it is more apparent than the relation in the first meaning. He called the first 'real' because it is opposite to the real particular. However, the fitness for assuming sharing among many may be disputed as being relative, even if its conception depends on conception of another, just as the conception of prevention from assuming sharing among many depends on conception of another even though it is not relative, because its realization does not depend on the realization of the other. Then its being called 'real' is apparent. According to this, the relative particular is that which is actually subsumed under something else.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage is a definitional analysis of two types of universals: the real universal (kulli haqiqi) and the relative universal (kulli idafi). The author begins by noting that while the distinction between real and relative for particulars is clear, for universals it is not immediately obvious. The real universal, as previously defined, is that which can be predicated of many, which itself seems relative because it involves relation to many. If that were all, there would be only one meaning. But the author, responding to this objection, explains that the relative universal is different: it is defined as 'that which is more general than a thing' (الأعم من شيء), meaning that something else is subsumed under it in reality, not merely by mental assumption. The real universal only requires the possibility of subsumption by the mind, while the relative universal requires actual subsumption. Two degrees of specificity are then enumerated: (1) the real universal may have no possible subsumption (like fictional universals), while the relative always has actual subsumption; (2) the real universal may allow possible subsumption even if not actual, while the relative requires actual subsumption. The naming is justified: the relative is so called because its relation is more manifest, and the real because it opposes the real particular. The passage ends by noting that the real universal's quality of being predicable of many is not necessarily relative, because its realization does not depend on an actual other, unlike the relative. This leads to a definition of the relative particular as that which is actually subsumed.

Key Terms
الكلي الحقيقي
الكلي الإضافي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the defining characteristic of the relative universal (al-kulli al-idafi)?
A) It can be predicated of many only in theory.
B) It is more general than the real universal.
C) Something is actually subsumed under it in reality.
D) It is the same as the real universal.

Key Takeaway
The real universal is defined by mental possibility of subsumption, while the relative universal requires actual subsumption in reality – a distinction critical for precise definition in Islamic sciences.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the term 'wajib' (obligatory) in fiqh. It is a universal that applies to many acts (prayer, fasting, etc.). Would you classify it as a real universal or a relative universal? Explain your reasoning using the two degrees of specificity.
?
Imagine a fiqh text says 'Every intoxicant is forbidden.' Is the term 'intoxicant' here a real universal or a relative universal? Cite the condition of actual subsumption.

The Two Degrees of Specificity: How the Relative Universal is More Specific
Enumerates two degrees of specificity of relative over real universal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to enumerate and explain the two degrees by which the relative universal is more specific than the real universal.

Core Idea
Two degrees of specificity: real universal may have no possible subsumption or only possible; relative has actual.

After establishing the basic distinction, the passage deepens the analysis by specifying two ways in which the relative universal is more restricted. Mastering these degrees refines your grasp of how universals relate to reality.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first degree
In the Arabic, find the first degree: the real universal may have no possibility of subsumption (e.g., fictional universals like 'winged horse'), while the relative universal always has actual subsumption. Understand that this is a stronger condition.
2
Identify the second degree
Find the second degree: the real universal may allow possible subsumption even if not actual (neither mentally nor externally), but the relative requires actual subsumption. Recognize that this covers cases where subsumption is possible but not realized.

There is a discussion, because the distinction between the particular and that one of them is real and the other relative is something manifest as he explained. As for the universal, it does not appear to have two distinct meanings likewise. But if he means another meaning, why did he not explain it? I say: He meant another meaning, and he explained it by his saying: 'It is the more general than a thing.' Two Defects in Defining the Relative Partial
Author critiques definition of relative partial

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two logical defects in defining a relative term and evaluate why they invalidate the definition.

Core Idea
A relative term cannot be defined by its own synonym or its correlate without circularity.

In this passage, the commentator al-Sharif al-Jurjani critiques a proposed definition of the relative partial (al-juz'ī al-iḍāfī) as 'the more specific than something'. He argues that this definition suffers from two interrelated defects: defining the term by itself or by what depends on its own knowledge, and defining it by its correlate or by what depends on the correlate's knowledge. Understanding these defects sharpens our ability to evaluate definitions in logic and other Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition under critique
Find the definition being examined: 'al-akhass min shay' (the more specific than something). Note that it is offered as a better alternative to previous attempts.
The definition is meant to define the relative partial, which is a particular concept relative to a universal.
2
Understand the principle of correlatives
The author states that the specific (al-khass) and the general (al-'amm) are correlatives (mutaḍāyifān). One correlative cannot be used in the definition of the other, because that would require prior knowledge of the definiendum.
Correlatives are pairs where each is understood relative to the other, like father and son.
3
Extract the first defect: self-definition
The phrase 'al-akhass' (more specific) is treated as synonymous with 'al-khass' (specific). Since the relative partial is itself the specific, this defines the thing by its synonym, which is equivalent to defining by itself – a circularity.
This defect is called 'ta'rif al-shay' bi nafsihi' (defining a thing by itself).
4
Extract the second defect: reliance on correlate
If 'al-akhass' is taken as different from 'al-khass' (i.e., the comparative, meaning 'more specific'), its conception depends on the conception of 'al-khass' (specific). But 'al-khass' is the correlate of 'al-'amm', which is involved in the definition. Thus the definition relies on what depends on the correlate's knowledge.
This second defect involves defining by a correlate indirectly.
5
Evaluate the defense and rejection
A defense claims that the author (al-muṣannif) mentioned both correlatives together, which is harmless. The commentator rejects this: if one admits the synonymy, the objection stands; if not, the definition is not the one proposed.
This shows the rigor required in logical definitions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مباحث الكلي والجزئي
الخاص خاص بالنسبة إلى العام، كذلك العام عام بالنسبة إلى الخاص وأحد المتضايفين لا يجوز أن يذكر في تعريف المتضايف الآخر، وإلا لكان تعقله قبل تعقله - لامعه - وأيضاً لفظة «كلّ» إنما هي للأفراد والتعريف بالأفراد ليس بجائز، فالأولى أن يقال هو الأخص من شيء. قلت: تعقل الأعمّ يتوقف على تعقل العام، الذي هو الإضافي مع أن المقصود بالأعم والأخص هاهنا هو العام والخاص، لا معنى التفضيل والزيادة في العموم والخصوص، لكن على هذا يلزم تعريف الجزئي الإضافي بالخاص الذي هو بمعناه، فيلزم تعريف الشيء بنفسه ومضايفه معاً ؛ وعلى الأول يلزم تعريفه بالأخص الذي يتوقف تعقله على تعقل الخاص، فيلزم تعريف الشيء بما يتوقف معرفته على معرفته وبما يتوقف على معرفة مضايفه، فالخلل في التعريف من وجهين : أحدهما تعريف الشيء بنفسه أو بما يتوقف على معرفته، والثاني تعريفه بمضايفه أو بما يتوقف على معرفة مضايفه ؛ ولاشك أن الخلل الأول أقوى من الثاني، فالأولى أن لا يقتصر على الثاني وحده. وأيضاً يلزم أن لا يكون تعريفه بالأخص من شيء - كما ذكره الشارح - صحيحاً لاشتماله على الخلل الأول قطعاً - هذا. وقد قيل في جواب النظر : إنّ المصنف ذكر المتضايفين معاً - أعني الأخص والأعم - في تعريف شيء واحد هو الجزئي الإضافي، ولا محذور في ذلك». وليس بشيء : لأن هذا القائل إن سلّم أن معنى الجزئي الإضافي هو الخاص ومعنى الكلّي الإضافي هو العام - كما ذكره الشارح - : فالنظر وارد مع زيادة كما عرفت؛ وإن لم يسلم : فالجواب هو ذاك، لا ما ذكره. (شريف)
Topics of the universal and the partial. The specific is specific relative to the general, likewise the general is general relative to the specific, and one of the two correlatives is not permissible to be mentioned in the definition of the other correlative, otherwise its conception would precede its conception - impossible. Also, the word 'every' is only for individuals, and definition by individuals is not permissible. So the better is to say: it is the more specific than something. I say: the conception of the more general depends on the conception of the general, which is relative, despite the fact that the intended meaning of 'more general' and 'more specific' here is the general and the specific, not the meaning of preference and increase in generality and specificity. But on this, it follows that the relative partial is defined by the specific which is its synonym, so it follows that the thing is defined by itself and its correlate together. On the first view, it follows that it is defined by the more specific whose conception depends on the conception of the specific, so it follows that the thing is defined by that whose knowledge depends on its own knowledge and by that whose knowledge depends on the knowledge of its correlate. So the defect in the definition is from two aspects: one is defining the thing by itself or by that which depends on its knowledge, and the second is defining it by its correlate or by that which depends on the knowledge of its correlate. There is no doubt that the first defect is stronger than the second, so it is better not to limit to the second alone. Also, it follows that its definition by 'the more specific than something' - as the commentator mentioned - is not correct, because it necessarily includes the first defect. This has been said. And it was said in answer to the objection: 'The author mentioned the two correlatives together - that is, the more specific and the more general - in the definition of one thing, namely the relative partial, and there is no harm in that.' And it is nothing, because if this speaker concedes that the meaning of relative partial is the specific and the meaning of relative universal is the general - as the commentator mentioned - then the objection holds with an addition as you know; and if he does not concede, then the answer is that, not what he mentioned. (Sharif)
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage is a critical commentary on the definition of the relative partial (al-juz'i al-idafi). The author begins with a general principle: the specific (al-khass) is specific relative to the general (al-'amm), and they are correlatives (mutadayifan). One correlative cannot be used in the definition of the other, otherwise circularity arises. Also, the word 'kull' (every) is used for individuals, and definition by enumeration of individuals is invalid. So the initial proposal 'it is the more specific than something' (al-akhass min shay) is considered. The author then objects: the conception of 'more specific' depends on the conception of 'specific', but the intended terms here are 'general' and 'specific' in their absolute sense, not the comparative. If we define relative partial by 'specific', that is synonymous, leading to defining the thing by itself and its correlate. If we define it by 'more specific', that depends on 'specific', which is its correlate, so the definition relies on what depends on the thing's knowledge and on the knowledge of its correlate. Thus two defects: (1) defining by itself or what depends on it, (2) defining by its correlate or what depends on that. The first is worse. The author then refutes a potential defense that the author (al-musannif) meant both correlatives in the definition of one thing, which is harmless. The rebuttal: if one accepts that relative partial is identical to specific, then the objection stands; if not, then the definition is not what was claimed. This sharpens the logical criteria for definitions.

Key Terms
الجزئي الإضافي (al-juz'ī al-iḍāfī): The relative partial: a particular concept that is under a broader universal, defined as the specific relative to a general. [Note: This term is stable in Mantiq; no significant shift.]
المتضايفان (al-mutaḍāyifān): Correlatives: two terms such that each conceptually depends on the other, like father and son. [Note: Stable across logic and language disciplines.]
الأخص (al-akhass): The more specific: comparative form referring to the more specific of two things, used synonymously with 'specific' in this context. [Note: In this passage, 'akhass' is treated as equivalent to 'khass' by the objector, but the commentator insists on distinction.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the critique, what are the two defects in defining the relative partial as 'al-akhass min shay'?
A) Defining by the same term and defining by a synonym
B) Defining by itself and defining by its correlate
C) Defining by an individual and defining by a universal
D) Defining by something more general and defining by something more specific

Key Takeaway
A valid definition must avoid circularity and reliance on correlates; the relative partial cannot be defined by 'the more specific than something' without committing these errors.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the definition: 'Knowledge (al-'ilm) is the conception of something as it is.' Does this definition involve defining by a correlate? Why or why not?
?
Examine the definition: 'Mujtahid is one who derives rulings from the sources.' Does it suffer from any of the two defects discussed? Identify any circularity or reliance on a correlate.

intermediate
5 min
Relative Partial is More General than Real Partial
Proof that every real partial is a relative partial.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to prove that every real partial is a relative partial by stripping individuators.

Core Idea
Every real partial is a relative partial.

The logicians distinguish between two types of partial: real (individual) and relative (falling under a universal). This lesson examines their relationship and the proof that the latter encompasses the former.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim
The claim is that 'the relative partial is more general than the real partial', meaning every real partial is a relative partial, but not every relative partial is real.
2
Examine the proof
Take a real partial like Zayd. Imagine stripping away all the individuating properties. What remains is the essence 'human', which is universal. This universal is more general than Zayd, so Zayd is subsumed under it, making him a relative partial.
The same reasoning applies to any individual.
3
Generalize
Since the stripped essence is always more general than the individual, every real partial is necessarily a relative partial.
This conclusion holds as long as the individual has a universal essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهو - أي الجزئي الإضافي - أعم من الجزئي الحقيقي، يعني أن كل جزئي حقيقي جزئي إضافي بدون العكس.
أما الأوّل فلأن كل جزئي حقيقي فهو مندرج تحت ماهيته المعراة عن المشخصات، كما إذا جردنا زيداً عن المشخصات التي بها صـار شخصاً معيناً بقيت الماهية الإنسانية وهي أعم منه، فيكون كل جزئي حقيقي مندرجاً تحت أعم، فيكون جزئياً إضافياً.
(۱
وهذا منقوض بواجب الوجود فإنّه شخص معين ويمتنع أن يكون له ماهيّة كلّيّة، وإلا فهو إن كان مجرد تلك الماهية الكلية يلزم أن يكون أمر واحد كلّيّاً وجزئيّاً وهو محال ، وإن كانت تلك الماهية مع شيء آخر يلزم . أن يكون واجب الوجود معروضاً للتشخص، وهو محال، لما تقرر في فن الحكمة أن تشخص واجب الوجود عينه.
(۱) أي بذاته المخصوصة المقدسة، لا بمفهومه، فإنه كلّي كما مرّ.
وأجيب عن هذا النقض بأن مناط الكلية والجزئية هو الوجود الذهني - كما صرح به - وليس من شأن الموجود المعين الذي هو الواجب الوجود لذاته أن يحصل في الذهن حتى يتصف بالجزئية ؛ بل لا يعقل إلا بوجوه تفرض كلية منحصرة في شخص. و ردّ بأن معنى الجزئي هو ما كان بحيث لو حصل في الذهن لمنع، وهذا معنى قولهم : «كل مفهوم إما أن يمنع ... الخ » إذ لم يريدوا به كونه مفهوماً بالفعل، وذلك لا يتوقف على الحصول بالفعل في الذهن ولا على إمكان حصوله فيه ؛ والجزئي الحقيقي بهذا المعنى يصدق على الواجب كما لا يخفي. وأيضاً الممتنع الحصول في الذهن هو كنه ذاته، لاذاته على وجه مخصوص تعرض له الجزئية (شريف).
And it - i.e., the relative partial - is more general than the real partial, meaning that every real partial is a relative partial but not vice versa. As for the first, because every real partial is subsumed under its essence stripped of individuators, just as if we strip Zayd of the individuators by which he became a particular person, the human essence remains and it is more general than him, so every real partial is subsumed under a more general, so it is a relative partial. (1) This is refuted by the Necessary Existence, for He is a particular person and it is impossible for Him to have a universal essence; otherwise, if He were merely that universal essence, it would follow that one thing is both universal and particular, which is impossible; and if that essence were with something else, it would follow that the Necessary Existence is a locus for individuation, which is impossible, because it is established in philosophy that the individuation of the Necessary Existence is His very essence. (1) i.e., by His specific sacred essence, not by His concept, for that is universal as previously. And this refutation was answered by saying that the criterion of universality and particularity is mental existence - as stated - and it is not the property of a specific existent like the Necessary Existence in His essence to occur in the mind so as to be described as particular; rather, He is only conceived by aspects that are hypothesized as universal confined to a person. And it was rebutted that the meaning of 'partial' is that which, if it were to occur in the mind, would prevent [others from sharing]; this is the meaning of their saying: 'Every concept either prevents... etc.' for they did not mean by it being an actual concept, and that does not depend on actual occurrence in the mind nor on the possibility of its occurrence; and the real partial in this sense applies to the Necessary Existence, as is not hidden. Also, what is impossible to occur in the mind is His quiddity, not His essence under a specific aspect that admits particularity. (Sharif)
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical expansion on the relationship between the relative partial (juz'i idafi) and the real partial (juz'i haqiqi). The author first asserts that the relative partial is more general than the real partial: every real partial is a relative partial, but not conversely. The proof: every real partial (like Zayd) can be stripped of its individuators (mushakhkhasat) to leave a universal essence (e.g., 'human'), which is more general than the individual; thus the individual falls under a universal, making it a relative partial. An objection is raised: the Necessary Existence (Wajib al-Wujud, i.e., God) is a particular person but cannot have a universal essence. If He did, He would be both universal and particular (contradiction), or would have accidental individuation (impossible, since His individuation is His essence). A marginal note clarifies that 'His specific sacred essence' is meant, not His concept. A first answer replies that universality/particularity are mental existence criteria, and the Necessary Existence cannot occur in the mind. A rebuttal refutes this: 'partial' is defined as what would prevent sharing if it occurred in the mind, regardless of actual occurrence; the real partial applies to the Necessary Existence in this sense. Also, what is impossible to conceive is His quiddity (kunh dhati), not His essence under a specific aspect. This shows the nuanced debate on whether God can be considered a partial.

Key Terms
الجزئي الحقيقي
الجزئي الإضافي
المشخصات

A) A different individual
B) The universal essence 'human'

D) Zayd's personal identity

Key Takeaway
Every real partial is a relative partial because it falls under its own universal essence after individuation is removed.

Take any real partial from Islamic law (e.g., 'this specific fasting on Ramadan day') and perform the mental stripping of its individuators (e.g., date, place, person) to identify the universal essence ('fasting') it falls under. Verify that it becomes a relative partial.

The Wajib al-Wujud Objection and Dialectical Responses
Dialectical exchange on whether God is a relative partial.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the objection that the Necessary Existence refutes the claim that every real partial is a relative partial, and evaluate the responses.

Core Idea
The case of God challenges the universality of the real-to-relative partial relationship.

The claim that every real partial is a relative partial faces a theological objection: God (Wajib al-Wujud) is a real partial but cannot have a universal essence. This lesson explores the dialectical exchange that follows, including two answers and a rebuttal.

Guided Path
1
State the objection
The objector argues: God is a real partial (particular individual), but He has no universal essence (quiddity) because His essence is His own individuation. Therefore, He cannot be subsumed under a universal, so He is not a relative partial. This counterexample would refute the claim.
2
Analyze the first answer
The first answer claims that the criterion of universality/particularity is mental existence. Since God cannot occur in the mind, He is not subject to these categories, so the objection fails.
This answer relies on a particular theory of the criterion.
3
Examine the rebuttal
The rebuttal counters that 'partial' is defined in terms of potentiality: if it were to occur in the mind, it would prevent sharing. This applies to God. Additionally, what is inconceivable is only His quiddity, not His essence under a specific aspect.
This rebuttal challenges the first answer's assumption.
4
Synthesize
The passage does not endorse a final resolution; it presents a dialectical standoff. This shows how logical principles interact with theological commitments.

Source Text

Real and Relative Species
Commentary defines the two types of species: real and relative.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between real species and relative species and identify each in a given example.

Core Idea
Species is either absolute (real) or relative to a genus; a relative species can also be a genus.

In this passage, the commentator expands on the fifth universal, species, by introducing a crucial distinction: species can be understood in two ways. The real species is the familiar one defined by a single essence. But there is also a relative species, which is species only in relation to a higher genus. This distinction helps avoid confusion when a term like 'human' can be both a species (under 'animal') and a genus (under nothing, since it is the lowest species). Let's unpack this carefully.

Guided Path
1
Identify the terms being defined
Find the two definitions in the Arabic: one for 'real species' (al-naw' al-haqiqi) and one for 'relative species' (al-naw' al-idafi). Notice the structure: both are species, but the condition differs.
The passage begins with 'al-khamis: al-naw'... and then contrasts the two.
2
Extract the defining conditions
For real species: it is predicated of many individuals that agree in essence (متفقين بالحقيقة). For relative species: it is an essence predicated together with another essence by the same genus in answer to 'What is it?' as a primary predication.
Primary predication means the genus directly answers the essence question.
3
Compare the two definitions
Real species is absolute: its species-ness comes from the single essence. Relative species is relative: it is species only in respect to a higher genus (it can also be a genus to lower species).
Example: 'human' is a real species because all humans share the same essence; it is also a relative species when considered under 'animal'.
4
Apply the distinction to an example
Take 'human'. Is it a real species? Yes, because it is predicated of Zayd and 'Amr who agree in essence. Is it a relative species? Yes, because 'human' is a species under the genus 'animal', and 'animal' is predicated of both 'human' and 'horse' in answer to 'What is it?'.
This shows that one term can be both real and relative species from different perspectives.
5
Test the definition's completeness
Check if the definition of relative species covers all instances. For example, 'animal' is not a relative species because it has no higher genus (it is a highest genus). Does the definition exclude such cases? Yes, because 'animal' is not predicated together with another by a higher genus.
The definition ensures that only intermediate universals are relative species.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال : الخامس: النوع كما يقال على ماذكرناه - ويقال له: «النوع الحقيقي» فكذلك يقال على كلّ ماهيّة يقال عليها وعلى غيرها الجنس في جواب «ما هو؟» قولا أولياً، ويسمّى «النوع الإضافي». القول : النوع كما يطلق على ماذكرناه - وهو «المقول على كثيرين متفقين بالحقيقة في جواب ما هو »، ويقال له : «النوع الحقيقي» لأنّ نوعيته إنما هي بالنظر إلى حقيقته الواحدة الحاصلة في أفراده - كذلك
He said: The fifth [universal]: species, just as it is said in the manner we mentioned - and it is called 'real species' - so too it is said of every essence that is predicated together with another essence by the genus in response to 'What is it?' as a primary predication, and it is called 'relative species'. The discourse: species, just as it is applied in the manner we mentioned - and it is 'predicated of many that are in agreement in reality in response to What is it?' - and it is called 'real species' because its species-ness is only by virtue of its single essence present in its individuals - likewise...
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage defines the fifth universal, namely species (al-naw'), and distinguishes its two types: real species and relative species. The author first restates the familiar definition of real species as 'predicated of many that are in agreement in reality in response to What is it?', which is the standard definition from the Isaghuji. This is called 'real species' because its species-ness is based on the single essence shared by its individuals. Then a second type is introduced: relative species, which is defined as every essence that is predicated together with another essence by the same genus in response to 'What is it?' as a primary predication. This means that a relative species is species only in relation to a higher genus, i.e., it is a species relative to that genus, while also being a genus relative to something else. The commentary here is brief but clarifies the distinction. The passage is from the commentary on the matn, so it is an expansion_probe.

Key Terms
النوع الحقيقي
النوع الإضافي
جواب ما هو

Key Takeaway
The fifth universal, species, is of two types: real species (absolute) and relative species (which is species only in relation to a higher genus).

Distinguishing Real and Relative Particulars
Author explains why relative particular can be universal while real particular cannot.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the real particular and the relative particular and explain why only the relative particular can be universal.

Core Idea
Some particulars can be universal when they are relative; real particulars are absolutely particular.

In Islamic logic, not all particulars are alike. The real particular is absolutely particular and cannot be predicated of many, but the relative particular is more specific than something else and can therefore fall under a higher universal. This passage clarifies this crucial distinction and its implications for the hierarchy of concepts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of particulars
Find in the Arabic text the terms 'al-juz'ī al-ḥaqīqī' (real particular) and 'al-juz'ī al-iḍāfī' (relative particular). Note that the real particular is defined as that which cannot be universal in any respect, while the relative particular is that which can be universal relative to something else.
2
Understand why the relative particular can be universal
The text states that the relative particular can be universal because it is 'more specific than something' (أخص من شيء). Anything that is more specific than something can itself be a universal under another, higher universal. For example, 'human' is more specific than 'animal', yet 'human' can be a universal for 'Zayd' and 'Amr'.
3
Contrast with the real particular
The real particular cannot be universal at all because it is absolutely particular; it cannot be predicated of many. The text says 'the real particular prevents' (يمتنع) universality.
4
Examine the relationships between particulars and universals
The passage outlines relationships: the real particular is in opposition (مباينة) to universals because it prevents predication, while the relative particular has a partial overlap (عموم من وجه) with universals because it can apply to some individuals that universals do not, and vice versa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما الثاني : فلجواز أن يكون الجزئي الإضافي كلّيّاً، لأنه الأخص من شيء، والأخص من شيء يجوز أن يكون كلياً تحت كلّي آخر، بخلاف الجزئي الحقيقي فإنه يمتنع أن يكون كليا. قد ظهر بما ذكره النسبة بين الجزئيين، وما ذكرت النسبة بين الكليين؛ وأما النسبة بين الجزئي الحقيقي وبين كل واحد من الكليين، فالمباينة لأن الجزئي يمنع والكلي لا يمنع ; وأما النسبة بين الجزئي الإضافي وبين كل واحد من بينهما : فالعموم من وجه لصدق الجزئي الإضافي على الجزئي الحقيقي بدونهما وصدقهما بدونه في المفهومات الشاملة، وتصادق الكلي على الكليات المتوسطة (شریف).
As for the second: because it is possible for the relative particular to be universal, because it is more specific than something, and what is more specific than something may be universal under another universal, unlike the real particular, for it cannot be universal. It has become clear from what he mentioned the relationship between the two particulars, and the relationship between the two universals was not mentioned; as for the relationship between the real particular and each of the two universals, it is opposition because the particular prevents and the universal does not prevent; as for the relationship between the relative particular and each of the two, it is general in one respect because the relative particular applies to the real particular without them, and they apply without it in comprehensive concepts, and the universal applies to the intermediate universals (Sharif).
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage distinguishes between the relative particular and the real particular. The relative particular can be universal because it is more specific than something else, and such a thing can fall under a higher universal. In contrast, the real particular cannot be universal at all. The commentary expands by explaining the relationships: the real particular and universals are mutually exclusive, while the relative particular has a partial overlap with universals. This distinction is crucial for understanding the hierarchy of universals and particulars in Islamic logic.

Key Terms
الجزئي الحقيقي
الجزئي الإضافي

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because the relative particular is not a real particular.
D) Because the real particular is not more specific than anything.

Key Takeaway
The relative particular is not absolutely particular; it can be universal under a higher universal, while the real particular cannot.

Real Species and Relative Species
Author defines the fifth universal, species, and its two types: real and relative.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish real species from relative species and explain how each is defined in terms of genus and quiddity.

Core Idea
Species is twofold: real when sharing essence, relative when sharing a genus with another quiddity.

In this passage, the author defines the fifth universal (species) and its two types. Real species covers things that share the same essence, while relative species covers quiddities that fall under a common genus. The commentary clarifies the relational nature of relative species and addresses an objection about the necessity of mentioning 'universal' in its definition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of species mentioned
Find the terms 'النوع الحقيقي' and 'النوع الإضافي' in the Arabic text. Note that both are called 'species' but with different meanings.
The author uses 'كذلك يطلق بالاشتراك' to indicate common usage.
2
Compare the definitions
Real species is predicated of many individuals that agree in reality (e.g., 'man' for Zayd and Amr). Relative species is a quiddity that, together with another quiddity, is answered under the same genus in response to 'what is it?'.
The relative species is defined by its relation to a higher genus, not by its own essence alone.
3
Analyze the example of man and animal
Man is a real species when considered in itself, but a relative species when considered alongside horse under the genus animal. The genus is predicated of both quiddities primarily.
The example shows how one quiddity can be both a real species and a relative species from different perspectives.
4
Understand the objection about universals
The objector argues that quiddities are mental forms and thus universals, so mentioning 'universal' is redundant. The response is that the relative species is defined by its relation to the genus, and the relation itself suffices; the universal aspect is implicit.
The objection and response clarify the logical precision required in definitions.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال : الخامس: النوع كما يقال على ماذكرناه - ويقال له: «النوع الحقيقي» فكذلك يقال على كلّ ماهيّة يقال عليها وعلى غيرها الجنس في جواب «ما هو؟» قولا أولياً، ويسمّى «النوع الإضافي». القول : النوع كما يطلق على ماذكرناه - وهو «المقول على كثيرين متفقين بالحقيقة في جواب ما هو »، ويقال له : «النوع الحقيقي» لأنّ نوعيته إنما هي بالنظر إلى حقيقته الواحدة الحاصلة في أفراده - كذلك يطلق بالاشتراك على كلّ ماهيّة يقال عليها وعلى غيرها «الجنس» في جواب ما هو ؟» قولاً أولياً - أي بلا واسطة - كالإنسان بالقياس إلى الحيوان، فإنّه ماهيّة يقال عليها وعلى غيرها كالفرس الجنس - وهو الحيوان - حتى إذا قيل : ما الإنسان والفرس ؟ فالجواب أنه حيوان ولهذا المعنى يسمّى «نوعاً إضافياً» لأن نوعيته بالإضافة إلى مافوقه، فالماهية منزلة منزلة الجنس، ولابد من ترك لفظ «كل» الماسمعت في مبحث الجزئي الإضافي من أن كل للأفراد، والتعريف للأفراد، ولا يجوز ذكر الكلي لأنه جنس الكليات، ولاتتمّ حدودها بدون ذكره. فإن قلت : الماهية هي الصورة المعقولة من الشيء، والصور العقلية كليات؛ فذكرها يغني عن ذكر الكلّي. G ماهو، فلاشك أن كل واحدة من تينك الماهيتين المندرجتين تحته موصوفة بأن يقال عليها وعلى غيرها الجنس في جواب ماهو، وهذه الصفة ثابتة لهما بالقياس إلى الجنس الذي اندرجت فيه، كما أن صفة الجنسية ثابتة للجنس بالقياس إلى ما اندرج تحته من الماهيات التي هي أنواع له؛ فالجنس والنوع المندرج تحته متضايفان - كالأب والابن (شريف).
He said: The fifth is species, as it is said in what we mentioned – and it is called 'real species' – likewise it is said of every quiddity that is said, and other than it, the genus in answer to 'what is it?' primarily, and it is called 'relative species'. The statement: Species, as it is applied to what we mentioned – and it is 'predicated of many agreeing in reality in answer to what is it?', and it is called 'real species' because its species-ness is only with respect to its single reality present in its individuals – likewise it is applied by common usage to every quiddity that is said, and other than it, the genus in answer to 'what is it?' primarily – i.e., without mediation – like man in relation to animal, for it is a quiddity said, and other than it like horse, the genus – which is animal – such that if it is said: What are man and horse? The answer is that it is animal, and for this meaning it is called 'relative species' because its species-ness is in addition to what is above it, so the quiddity takes the place of the genus, and it is necessary to omit the word 'every' (or 'universal'?) as heard in the topic of relative particular, from that every (or 'the universal') is for individuals, and the definition is for individuals, and it is not permissible to mention the universal because it is the genus of universals, and their definitions are not completed without it. If you say: The quiddity is the mental form of the thing, and mental forms are universals; so mentioning it suffices from mentioning the universal. He said: What is it? For there is no doubt that each one of those two quiddities subsumed under it is described as being said, and other than it, the genus in answer to what is it, and this attribute is established for them relative to the genus under which they are subsumed, just as the attribute of genus-ness is established for the genus relative to what is subsumed under it of quiddities that are species for it; so the genus and the species subsumed under it are correlatives – like father and son (Sharif).
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage defines the two types of species. Real species (al-nawʿ al-ḥaqīqī) is predicated of many individuals that share the same reality, like 'man' for Zayd and Amr. Relative species (al-nawʿ al-iḍāfī) is a quiddity that, together with another quiddity, falls under a higher genus; e.g., 'man' and 'horse' both fall under 'animal'. The commentary explains that the relative species takes the place of the genus in relation to its own individuals, and the term 'universal' must be omitted from its definition to avoid redundancy. A potential objection is raised: since quiddities are mental forms and thus universals, why need we mention 'universal'? The answer is that the relative species is defined by its relation to a genus, and this relation alone suffices; the universal aspect is implicit. The genus and species are correlatives.

Why 'Universal' Must Be in Definitions of Relative Species
Commentator explains why 'universal' must be mentioned in definitions of relative species.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between relative species and real species, and explain why the term 'universal' is necessary in the definition of relative species.

Core Idea
Relative species has two relations; defining it requires including the genus 'universal'.

In logic, the five universals are defined nominally, not by mere description. When defining relative species (al-naw' al-idafi), the term 'universal' (kulli) must be mentioned because it serves as the genus. This lesson unpacks the commentator's reasoning, showing how relative species differs from real species.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of species
Recognize that there are two types of species: real species (al-naw' al-haqiqi) and relative species (al-naw' al-idafi). Real species is a universal predicated of many, like 'human'. Relative species is a universal that is itself a species of a higher genus.
This distinction is crucial for definitions of universals.
2
Understand nominal definitions
Definitions of universals are nominal (ḥadd ismī), meaning they must include the genus. This is opposed to mere descriptions (rusūm) which can omit the genus. Nominal definitions are complete.
The commentator stresses this to justify why 'universal' must be mentioned.
3
Note the two relations of relative species
If 'universal' is considered in the concept of relative species, the species has two relations: one to its individuals (since it is universal) and another to its genus above it (since it is a species). Real species has only the relation to its individuals.
This double relation is the key distinguishing feature.
4
Verify definition completeness
Because the definition is nominal, it must be complete. Mentioning the genus 'universal' ensures both relations are captured, making the definition complete. Without it, the definition would be deficient.
Completeness means the definition includes all essential parts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱) هذا إشارة إلى ما سبق من أن المذكور في تعريفات الكليات حدود اسمية لها لا رسوم كما توهم - وإذا كانت حدوداً كانت تامة كما هو الظاهر، فلابد حينئذ من ذكر الجنس - أعني الكلي - هاهنا رعاية لطريقة القوم في تعريف الكليات، وإذا اعتبر الكلّي في مفهوم النوع الاضافي كان فيه إضافتان : إحداهما بالقياس إلى ما تحته من أفراده لكونه كليّاً، والأخرى بالقياس إلى الجنس الذي فوقه كما بينا، والنوع الحقيقي فيه إضافة واحدة بالقياس إلى ما تحته فقط كما عرفت (شریف).
(1) This is an indication to what preceded: that what is mentioned in the definitions of universals are nominal definitions for them, not descriptions as was imagined – and if they are definitions, they are complete as is apparent, so it is necessary then to mention the genus – I mean the universal – here, observing the method of the people in defining universals. And if the universal is considered in the concept of relative species, then there are two additions: one relative to what is beneath it of its individuals because it is universal, and the other relative to the genus above it as we explained. And the real species has only one addition relative to what is beneath it only, as you know (Sharif).
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage clarifies why the term 'universal' must be mentioned in the definition of relative species. The commentator (Sharif) notes that the definitions of the five universals are nominal definitions (ḥudūd ismiyya), not mere descriptions. As such, they require the mention of the genus, which is 'universal'. For relative species, the inclusion of 'universal' introduces two relations: one to its individuals (as a universal) and one to its genus (as a species). Real species, in contrast, has only the relation to its individuals. This distinction ensures the definitions are complete.

Key Takeaway
Relative species requires mentioning the genus 'universal' in its definition because it has two relations: to its individuals and to its genus, unlike real species which has only one relation.

Genus as Relative Species: Conditions and Predication
Author defines genus as relative species with conditions of primary predication and universal inclusion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions for a quiddity to be considered a genus (relative species) and apply them to examples from Islamic logic.

Core Idea
Genus is a quiddity predicated of itself and others in answer to 'what is it?' with primary predication.

In this lesson, we examine the precise definition of 'jins' (genus) as it functions in the hierarchy of five universals. The author clarifies that genus is not simply a higher universal but a relative species (naw' idafi) with specific conditions. We will walk through these conditions, including the requirement of primary predication and the explicit inclusion of the universal, and understand why differentia, property, and common accident are excluded.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum
Find what is being defined: 'jins' (genus) in the sense of relative species (naw' idafi). The passage defines it as a quiddity said of itself and others in answer to 'what is it?' with primary predication.
The definition targets the logical genus, not the biological genus.
2
Extract the genus and differentia of the definition
The definition uses 'quiddity' as a broader category (genus proximum) and the conditions 'said of itself and others in answer to what is it?' and 'primary predication' as differentiae. Note that 'primary predication' distinguishes direct predication from mediated predication.
3
Understand primary predication
Primary predication means the term is applied without an intermediary. For example, 'animal' is said of 'human' directly, but when said of Zayd, it is via 'human'. In the definition of genus, only the immediate predication matters.
The hierarchy of universals shows that higher genera are predicated via lower ones.
4
Analyze the exclusions
The condition 'in answer to what is it?' excludes differentia, property, and common accident because they answer 'what kind of thing is it?' or 'what is its characteristic?' rather than 'what is its essence?'.
This ensures the definition captures the essence (whatness), not accidental features.
5
Understand why the universal must be mentioned
The author argues that quiddity (mahiyya) does not automatically imply universality; universality is a necessary concomitant. Since indication by concomitant is not accepted in definitions, the universal must be explicitly stated.
This prevents ambiguity and ensures the definition is complete.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يطلق بالاشتراك على كلّ ماهيّة يقال عليها وعلى غيرها «الجنس» في جواب ما هو؟» قولاً أولياً - أي بلا واسطة - كالإنسان بالقياس إلى الحيوان، فإنّه ماهيّة يقال عليها وعلى غيرها كالفرس الجنس - وهو الحيوان - حتى إذا قيل : ما الإنسان والفرس ؟ فالجواب أنه حيوان ولهذا المعنى يسمّى «نوعاً إضافياً» لأن نوعيته بالإضافة إلى مافوقه، فالماهية منزلة منزلة الجنس، ولابد من ترك لفظ «كل» الماسمعت في مبحث الجزئي الإضافي من أن كل للأفراد، والتعريف للأفراد، ولا يجوز ذكـر الكلي لأنه جنس الكليات، ولاتتمّ حدودها بدون ذكره. فإن قلت : الماهية هي الصورة المعقولة من الشيء، والصور العقلية كليات؛ فذكرها يغني عن ذكر الكلّي. فنقول: الماهية ليس مفهومها مفهوم الكلّي، غاية ما في الباب أنه من لوازمها، فتكون دلالة الماهية على الكلّي دلالة الملزوم على اللازم، يعني دلالة الالتزام، لكن دلالة الالتزام مهجورة في التعريفات. وقوله : « في جواب ماهو ؟ » يُخرج الفصل والخاصة والعرض العام، فإن الجنس لا يقال عليها وعلى غيرها في جواب ما هو. وأم تقييد القول بـ «الأولي» فاعلم أولا أن سلسلة الكليات إنما تنتهي بالأشخاص وهو النوع المقيد بالتشخص، وفوقها الأصناف وهو النوع المقيد بصفات عرضية كلية - كالرومي والتركي - وفوقها الأنواع، وفوقها الأجناس؛ وإذا حمل كليات مرتبة على شيء واحد يكون حمل العالي عليه بواسطة حمل السافل عليه، فإنّ الحيوان إنما يصدق على زيد وعلى التركي بواسطة حمل الإنسان عليهما وحمل الحيوان على الإنسان.
Genus is applied metaphorically to every quiddity that is said of it and of others in answer to 'What is it?' as a primary predication—i.e., without intermediary—like 'human' in relation to 'animal', for it is a quiddity said of it and of others like 'horse' of the genus—which is 'animal'—so that if one asks: 'What are human and horse?' then the answer is 'animal'. And for this meaning it is called 'relative species' because its species-ness is relative to what is above it. So the quiddity is placed in the position of the genus. And it is necessary to leave out the word 'every' [kull] as heard in the discussion of the particular relative [juz'i idafi] from the fact that 'every' is for individuals, and the definition is for individuals, and it is not permissible to mention the universal because it is the genus of universals, and their definitions are not complete without mentioning it. If you say: 'Quiddity is the intelligible form of a thing, and intelligible forms are universals; so mentioning it suffices instead of mentioning the universal.' We say: The concept of quiddity is not the concept of the universal; the most that can be said is that it is one of its concomitants. So the indication of quiddity of the universal is the indication of the necessary condition of the necessary, meaning indication of implication, but indication of implication is abandoned in definitions. And His saying: 'in answer to "What is it?"' excludes differentia, property, and common accident, for genus is not said of them and of others in answer to 'What is it?'. And as for the restriction of the predication to 'primary', know first that the hierarchy of universals ends with individuals, which is species restricted by particularization, and above them are kinds [asnaf], which is species restricted by accidental universal attributes—like Roman and Turk—and above them are species, and above them are genera. And when hierarchically ordered universals are predicated of one thing, the higher is predicated of it by means of the predication of the lower upon it, for 'animal' is only true of Zayd and of the Turk by means of the predication of 'human' upon them and the predication of 'animal' upon 'human'.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage is a definitional exposition from a commentary on the Shamsiyya, focusing on the concept of genus (jins) in the sense of relative species (naw' idafi). The author begins by defining genus as a quiddity that is predicated of itself and of others in answer to 'what is it?' with a primary predication—meaning without an intermediary. The example given is 'human' in relation to 'animal': both 'human' and 'horse' are said to be 'animal', so 'animal' is the genus relative to them. Because of this relative nature, such a quiddity is called 'relative species' since its species-ness is relative to a higher genus. The author then stresses the need to include the universal (al-kulli) in the definition, explaining that the word 'every' (kull) is not used because it pertains to individuals, but the definition of universals requires mentioning the universal itself. An objection is raised: since quiddity (mahiyya) is an intelligible form and all intelligible forms are universals, why not just mention quiddity? The response distinguishes the concept of quiddity from the concept of universal; universality is a necessary concomitant (lazim) of quiddity, and indication by concomitant (dalalat al-iltizam) is not accepted in definitions, so the universal must be explicitly stated. Next, the condition 'in answer to 'what is it?'' excludes differentia (fasl), property (khassa), and common accident ('arad 'amm) because these are not said in answer to 'what is it?' in the same way. Finally, the condition 'primary predication' (qawl awwali) is explained through the hierarchy of universals: higher universals are predicated of individuals only via lower universals. For example, 'animal' is true of Zayd only because 'human' is first predicated of him, and then 'animal' of 'human'. This hierarchy shows the primary nature of the predication in the definition.

Key Terms
الجنس
نوع إضافي
قول أولي
ماهية

C) Because quiddity is not universal.
D) Because it excludes differentia and property.

Key Takeaway
Genus is a relative species defined by primary predication and explicit universality; conditions exclude differentia, property, and common accident.

Defining Relative Species and the Condition of Primary Predication
Tahzeeb defines relative species and explains a key condition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of relative species and explain why the condition of primary predication was introduced to exclude subordinate genera.

Core Idea
Relative species is defined by a condition that critics argued makes it too restrictive.

This passage from Tahzeeb al-Mantiq introduces the term 'relative species' (النوع الإضافي) and a key condition: primary predication (القول الأولي). This condition is meant to exclude subordinate genera (الصنف) from the definition. However, as we will see, the condition has a serious flaw that later commentators addressed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
Find the definition of 'relative species' in the Arabic. The passage begins by explaining the phrase 'primary predication' as part of the definition.
The definition is not given in one sentence; it emerges through the discussion of the condition.
2
Understand the condition of primary predication
The condition 'primary' (أولي) is used to exclude subordinate genera. A subordinate genus is a universal that is predicated of its individuals not directly, but through an intermediate species. For example, 'animal' is predicated of 'Turk' and 'horse' through the species 'human' and 'horse'.
The commentator gives the example of asking about a Turk and a horse: the answer 'animal' is not primary because it comes via the species.
3
Extract the initial definition
From the text, the definition with the condition is: 'A universal that is predicated in answer to "what is it?" primarily, and upon which and upon others the genus is predicated in answer to "what is it?"'.
This is the definition before the critique.
4
Recognize the critique's starting point
The condition of primary predication, while excluding subordinate genera, also excludes species from being predicated of remote genera. For example, 'man' would not be a species of 'growing body' or 'substance' because the predication is not primary.
This creates a contradiction because man is called 'species of species' for being a species of all genera above it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أوّلي ، فقوله : «قولاً أولياً» احتراز عن الصنف، فإنّه كلّي يقال عليه وعلى غيره الجنس في جواب ما هو، حتى إذا سئل عن التركي والفرس بـ«ماهما»؟ كان الجواب : «الحيوان لكن قول الجنس على الصنف ليس بأولي، بل بواسطة حمل النوع عليه، فاعتبار الأولية في القول يخرج الصنف عن الحد، لأنه يسمّى نوعاً إضافياً.
٣٢- مراتب النوع الإضافي]
قال: ومراتبه أربع لأنه أما أعمّ الأنواع وهو «النوع العالي» كالجسم. أو أخصها وهو النوع السافل كالإنسان ويسمى «نوع الأنواع». أواعم من السافل وأخص من العالي وهو «النوع المتوسط» كالحيوان والجسم النامي. أو مباين للكل وهو النوع المفرد كالعقل - إن قلنا أن الجوهر جنس له.
(1) هذا القيد وإن أخرج الصنف عن الحد أخرج النوع عنه أيضاً بالقياس إلى الأجناس البعيدة، فيلزم أن لا يكون الإنسان» نوعاً للجسم النامي ، ولا للجسم ولا للجوهر ، مع أنه يسمّى «نوع الأنواع» لكونه نوعاً لكل واحد من الأنواع التي فوقه. وأيضاً النوع لما كان مضايفاً للجنس، فإذا اعتبر في النوع «القول الأولي» فلابد من اعتباره في الجنس أيضاً، وإلا لم يكن مضايفاله، فيلزم أن لا تكون الأجناس البعيدة أجناساً للماهية التي هي بعيدة بالقياس إليها، فالأولى أن يترك قيد «الأولية» ويُخرج الصنف بقيد آخر ويقال : «النوع الإضافي كلّي مقول في جواب «ماهو ؟» يقال عليه وعلى غيره الجنس في جواب ماهو» (شریف).
So his saying: 'a primary predication' is a precaution against the subordinate genus, for it is a universal that is predicated of itself and of others by the genus in answer to 'what is it?' such that when asked about the Turk and the horse 'what are they?', the answer is 'animal'. But the predication of the genus upon the subordinate genus is not primary; rather, it is through the mediation of the species being predicated of it. So considering primary in predication excludes the subordinate genus from the definition, because it is called a relative species.
[32- Ranks of relative species]
He said: and its ranks are four: for it is either the most general of species, which is the 'highest species' like body; or the most specific, which is the 'lowest species' like man, and it is called 'species of species'; or more general than the lowest and more specific than the highest, which is the 'intermediate species' like animal and the growing body; or separate from all, which is the 'unique species' like intellect – if we say that substance is a genus for it.
(1) This condition, although it excludes the subordinate genus from the definition, also excludes the species from it with respect to the remote genera. Consequently, man would not be a species for the growing body, nor for body, nor for substance, while he is called 'species of species' because he is a species for each of the species above him. Also, since species is correlative to genus, if the 'primary predication' is considered in species, it must also be considered in genus; otherwise they would not be correlatives. Consequently, remote genera would not be genera for the essence that is remote with respect to them. So it is better to abandon the condition of 'primary' and exclude the subordinate genus by another condition, and say: 'Relative species is a universal that is predicated in answer to "what is it?" and genus is predicated of it and of others in answer to "what is it?"' (Sharif).
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage defines relative species (النوع الإضافي) and then enumerates its four ranks. It begins by explaining the condition of 'primary predication' (القول الأولي) intended to exclude the subordinate genus (الصنف) from the definition of species. The commentator gives an example: when asked about a Turk and a horse, the answer is 'animal', but animal is predicated of these subordinate genera not directly but through the mediation of the species (e.g., human, horse). Thus primary predication excludes subordinate genera. The text then presents the four ranks of relative species: the highest species (النوع العالي) which has no genus above it, like body; the lowest species (النوع السافل) which has no species below it, like man, called 'species of species'; the intermediate species (النوع المتوسط) which is between them, like animal or growing body; and the unique species (النوع المفرد) which is neither above nor below, like intellect if substance is its genus. After this, a critical note is added: the condition of primary predication, while excluding subordinate genera, also excludes species from being predicated of remote genera. For example, man would not be a species of growing body or substance, yet man is called 'species of species' because it is a species for all genera above it. Furthermore, since species is correlative to genus, if primary predication is applied to species, it must also apply to genus; otherwise they would not be correlatives. Therefore, the commentator (al-Sharif) suggests dropping the condition of primary predication and instead excluding subordinate genera by a different condition, redefining relative species as a universal that is predicated in answer to 'what is it?' and upon which and upon others the genus is predicated in answer to 'what is it?'.

Key Terms
النوع الإضافي
القول الأولي
الصنف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the condition of 'primary predication' (القول الأولي) added to the definition of relative species?
A) To include subordinate genera
B) To exclude subordinate genera
C) To make the definition more general
D) To include real species

Key Takeaway
The condition of primary predication is intended to exclude subordinate genera, but it creates problems for the hierarchy of species, leading to a refined definition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In the definition of 'salah' as 'specific sayings and actions beginning with takbir and ending with taslim', identify the genus and differentia. Does this definition satisfy primary predication? Explain.
?
Consider the definition of 'sawm' (fasting) as 'abstention from food, drink, and sexual intercourse from dawn to sunset with intention'. Why might a condition like primary predication be needed to exclude invalid types of abstention?
